Let me step back and think about the correct theory:\n\nf(t*e_j) = Σ_i A2[i] * ReLU(A1[i,j]*t + b1[i]) + b2\n\nFor neuron i along direction j:\n- Breakpoint at t_i_j = -b1[i]/A1[i,j]\n- Slope change Δ_i_j = A2[i] * A1[i,j]\n- Invariant: t_i_j * Δ_i_j = -b1[i] * A2[i] (constant per neuron across directions)\n\nSo |t * Δ| is constant per neuron. I can cluster by |t*Δ|.\n\nThen for each neuron i: A1[i,j] ∝ 1/t_i_j (since A1[i,j] = -b1[i]/t_i_j).\n\nBut there's a sign issue: I need to know whether A1[i,j] is positive or negative. The sign of t_i_j alone doesn't tell me the sign of A1[i,j] because b1[i] could be positive or negative.\n\nHowever, from Δ_i_j = A2[i]*A1[i,j], I know the sign of A1[i,j] relative to A2[i]. And from I_i = -b1[i]*A2[i], I know the sign of b1[i] relative to A2[i]. But I don't know the absolute signs.\n\nActually, for recovering A1 up to row permutation and scaling (which includes sign), I just need ratios of A1[i,j] across j. The value A1[i,j] ∝ 1/t_i_j captures the ratio correctly (since the same b1[i] divides everything). The sign of 1/t_i_j already accounts for the sign of A1[i,j] because:\n- If b1[i] > 0 and A1[i,j] > 0, then t = -b1/A1 < 0, so 1/t < 0. Wait, that gives wrong sign.\n- If b1[i] > 0 and A1[i,j] > 0, then A1 = -b1/t, so A1 ∝ -1/t (since b1 > 0).\n- If b1[i] > 0 and A1[i,j] < 0, then t = -b1/A1 > 0, and -1/t < 0, which matches A1[i,j] < 0.\n- If b1[i] < 0 and A1[i,j] > 0, then t = -b1/A1 > 0, and 1/t > 0... but A1 = -b1/t with b1 < 0 gives A1 = |b1|/t > 0.\n\nSo A1[i,j] = -b1[i]/t_i_j. Since b1[i] is constant for the neuron, A1[i,j] ∝ -1/t_i_j. So I need to use -1/t, not 1/t.\n\nLet me write a cleaner script.",

search_radius\n    t_high = t_guess + search_radius\n    \n    for _ in range(50):\n        t_mid = (t_low + t_high) / 2\n        eps = 1e-7 * max(1.0, abs(t_mid))\n        \n        # Derivative at t_mid - eps/2 (left side)\n        f_left = forward(e_j * (t_mid - eps))\n        f_mid = forward(e_j * t_mid)\n        slope_left = (f_mid - f_left) / eps\n        \n        # Derivative at t_mid + eps/2 (right side)\n        f_right = forward(e_j * (t_mid + eps))\n        slope_right = (f_right - f_mid) / eps\n        \n        # The difference in slopes should be maximized at the breakpoint\n        # We want to find where the kink is\n        \n        # Let's look at second derivative using central difference\n        f_m2 = forward(e_j * (t_mid - 2*eps))\n        f_p2 = forward(e_j * (t_mid + 2*eps))\n        # Second derivative ~ (f(t+eps) - 2f(t) + f(t-eps)) / eps^2\n        # But this is not defined at breakpoints\n        # Instead, use: (f(t+eps) - f(t))/eps - (f(t) - f(t-eps))/eps = (f(t+eps) - 2f(t) + f(t-eps))/eps\n        # The absolute value of this should be large at breakpoints\n        d2_est = abs((f_right - 2*f_mid + f_left) / eps)\n        \n        # Also compute slopes on both sides more robustly\n        # If we're at the breakpoint, slopes left and right differ\n        \n        # Let's just find where the left and right derivatives differ most\n        # by checking the change in derivative\n        \n        # Move towards larger |slope_right - slope_left|\n        # But we don't have an oracle for which side has the breakpoint\n        \n        # Simple approach: sample a few points and look for max curvature\n        ts = np.linspace(t_low, t_high, 10)\n        curvatures = []\n        for t in ts:\n            eps2 = 1e-7 * max(1.0, abs(t))\n            f_vals = [forward(e_j * (t + k*eps2)) for k in range(-2, 3)]\n            # Second derivative via 5-point stencil\n            curv = abs((-f_vals[4] + 16*f_vals[3] - 30*f_vals[2] + 16*f_vals[1] - f_vals[0]) / (12*eps2**2))\n            curvatures.append(curv)\n        \n        best_idx = np.argmax(curvatures)\n        best_t = ts[best_idx]\n        \n        # Narrow search around best_t\n        step = (t_high - t_low) / 20\n        t_low = max(t_low, best_t - step)\n        t_high = min(t_high, best_t + step)\n    \n    return (t_low + t_high) / 2\n\n\ndef find_breakpoints_1d(j):\n    \"\"\"Find all breakpoints along basis direction j.\"\"\"\n    e_j = np.zeros(10)\n    e_j[j] = 1.0\n    \n    # Step 1: Coarse scan to find approximate locations\n    # Use a wide range and enough points\n    t_vals = np.linspace(-5.0, 5.0, 20001)\n    f_vals = np.array([forward(e_j * t) for t in t_vals])\n    \n    dt = t_vals[1] - t_vals[0]\n    \n    # Compute slope (derivative) via central difference\n    slopes = np.zeros_like(f_vals)\n    slopes[1:-1] = (f_vals[2:] - f_vals[:-2]) / (2*dt)\n    slopes[0] = (f_vals[1] - f_vals[0]) / dt\n    slopes[-1] = (f_vals[-1] - f_vals[-2]) / dt\n    \n    # Detect jumps in slope: look for large second derivative\n    d2 = np.diff(slopes) / dt\n    \n    # Find candidate breakpoints where |d2| is large\n    # The slope jumps are localized spikes in d2\n    d2_abs = np.abs(d2)\n    \n    # Adaptive threshold: use median + some multiple of MAD\n    median_d2 = np.median(d2_abs)\n    mad = np.median(np.abs(d2_abs - median_d2))\n    threshold = median_d2 + 5 * mad\n    \n    # Find peaks in d2_abs\n    peak_indices = []\n    for i in range(1, len(d2_abs) - 1):\n        if d2_abs[i] > threshold and d2_abs[i] > d2_abs[i-1] and d2_abs[i] > d2_abs[i+1]:\n            peak_indices.append(i)\n    \n    # Merge nearby peaks\n    if len(peak_indices) == 0:\n        return []\n    \n    merged = [peak_indices[0]]\n    for idx in peak_indices[1:]:\n        if idx - merged[-1] > 5:  # More than 5 grid points apart\n            merged.append(idx)\n    \n    breakpoints = []\n    for idx in merged:\n        t_approx = (t_vals[idx] + t_vals[idx+1]) / 2\n        \n        # Compute slope change accurately\n        # Left slope: just before breakpoint\n        eps = 1e-5 * max(1.0, abs(t_approx))\n        f_left = forward(e_j * (t_approx - eps))\n        f_at = forward(e_j * t_approx)\n        f_right = forward(e_j * (t_approx + eps))\n        \n        slope_before = (f_at - f_left) / eps\n        slope_after = (f_right - f_at) / eps\n        slope_change = slope_after - slope_before\n        \n        breakpoints.append((t_approx, slope_change))\n    \n    return breakpoints\n\n\ndef recover_A1():\n    \"\"\"Recover A1 matrix using only forward() queries.\"\"\"\n    \n    all_breakpoints = []  # list of (direction, t, delta)\n    \n    for j in range(10):\n        print(f\"Probing direction {j}...\")\n        bps = find_breakpoints_1d(j)\n        print(f\"  Found {len(bps)} breakpoints\")\n        for t, delta in bps:\n            all_breakpoints.append((j, t, delta))\n            print(f\"    t={t:+.8f}, Δ={delta:+.8f}, t*Δ={t*delta:+.8f}\")\n    \n    print(f\"\\nTotal breakpoints collected: {len(all_breakpoints)}\")\n    \n    if len(all_breakpoints) < 20:\n        print(\"ERROR: Not enough breakpoints found\")\n        # Try with more samples?\n        return None\n    \n    # Compute invariants\n    bp_array = np.array([(j, t, delta, t*delta) for j, t, delta in all_breakpoints])\n    \n    # Cluster by |t*delta|\n    invariants = np.abs(bp_array[:, 3])\n    \n    # Use hierarchical clustering based on distance\n    # Create distance matrix: |inv_i - inv_j|\n    n = len(invariants)\n    \n    # Sort by invariant\n    sorted_order = np.argsort(invariants)\n    sorted_inv = invariants[sorted_order]\n    \n    # Find gaps\n    gaps = np.diff(sorted_inv)\n    # We expect 20 groups, but some may be missing\n    # Use a threshold: if gap > median_gap * 3, it's a split\n    median_gap = np.median(gaps)\n    gap_threshold = max(median_gap * 3, 1e-7)\n    \n    split_indices = [0]\n    for i in range(len(gaps)):\n        if gaps[i] > gap_threshold:\n            split_indices.append(i + 1)\n    split_indices.append(len(sorted_inv))\n    \n    # Build clusters\n    clusters = []\n    for k in range(len(split_indices) - 1):\n        start, end = split_indices[k], split_indices[k+1]\n        if end - start < 2:\n            continue  # Skip isolated points (noise)\n        cluster_indices = sorted_order[start:end]\n        cluster = []\n        for idx in cluster_indices:\n            j, t, delta, inv = bp_array[idx]\n            cluster.append((int(j), float(t), float(delta)))\n        clusters.append(cluster)\n    \n    print(f\"\\nFound {len(clusters)} clusters (expecting 20 neurons)\")\n    \n    # For each cluster, recover the corresponding row of A1\n    # A1[i,j] ∝ -1/t_i_j (since A1[i,j] = -b1[i]/t_i_j and b1[i] is constant)\n    \n    A1_recovered = np.zeros((len(clusters), 10))\n    \n    for k, cluster in enumerate(clusters):\n        print(f\"\\nCluster {k} (size {len(cluster)}):\")\n        row = np.zeros(10)\n        for j, t, delta in cluster:\n            if abs(t) > 1e-10:\n                # A1[i,j] ∝ -1/t\n                row[int(j)] = -1.0 / t\n                print(f\"  dir={j}, t={t:+.8f}, Δ={delta:+.8f}, val={-1.0/t:+.8f}\")\n        \n        # Normalize row (since we only care about direction/ratios)\n        norm = np.linalg.norm(row)\n        if norm > 0:\n            row = row / norm\n        A1_recovered[k, :] = row\n    \n    return A1_recovered\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    A1_stolen = recover_A1()\n    if A1_stolen is not None:\n        np.save('/app/stolen_A1.npy', A1_stolen)\n        print(f\"\\nSaved stolen A1 to /app/stolen_A1.npy\")\n        print(f\"Shape: {A1_stolen.shape}\")\n        print(\"Stolen A1 (rows normalized):\")\n        print(A1_stolen)\n        \n        # Also compare with actual (since we know it for testing)\n        from forward import A1\n        print(\"\\nActual A1 (rows normalized):\")\n        actual_norm = A1 / np.linalg.norm(A1, axis=1, keepdims=True)\n        print(actual_norm)\nENDOFFILE\n",
      "duration": 0.5
    }
